id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div>\n\t<div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n\t</div>\n\t<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" >Enlargement of the European Union</h1>\n\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t<div id="contentSub2"></div>\n\t\t\n\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\n\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Accession process of new countries to the European Union</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif/300px-EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif" decoding="async" width="300" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif/450px-EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif/600px-EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The territories of the member states of the European Union (European Communities pre-1993), animated in order of accession. Territories outside Europe and its immediate surroundings are not shown.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) has expanded a number of times throughout its history by way of the accession of new <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member states</a> to the Union.  To join the EU, a state needs to fulfil economic and political conditions called the <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_criteria" title="Copenhagen criteria">Copenhagen criteria</a> (after the <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> summit in June 1993), which require a stable democratic government that respects the rule of law, and its corresponding freedoms and institutions. According to the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a>, each current member state and the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> must agree to any enlargement.  The process of enlargement is sometimes referred to as <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a>. This term is also used to refer to the intensification of co-operation between EU member states as national governments allow for the gradual harmonisation of national laws.\n</p><p>The EU\'s predecessor, the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> was founded with the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Six" title="Inner Six">Inner Six</a> member states in 1958, when the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">Treaty of Rome</a> came into force. Since then, the EU\'s membership has grown to twenty-seven, with the latest member state being <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, which joined in July 2013.  The most recent <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_European_Union" title="Geography of the European Union">territorial enlargement of the EU</a> was the incorporation of <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a> in 2014. The most notable <a href="/wiki/Withdrawal_from_the_European_Union" title="Withdrawal from the European Union">territorial reductions of the EU</a>, and its predecessors, have been the exit of <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> upon independence in 1962, the <a href="/wiki/Greenland%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Greenland\xe2\x80\x93European Union relations">exit of Greenland</a> in 1985, and the <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">withdrawal of the United Kingdom</a> in 2020.\n</p><p>As of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, accession negotiations are under way with <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> (since 2020), <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> (since 2012), <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a> (since 2020), <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> (since 2014) and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> (since 2005).  Serbia and Montenegro have been described by former <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">President of the European Commission</a> <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker" title="Jean-Claude Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</a> and Enlargement commissioner <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Hahn" title="Johannes Hahn">Johannes Hahn</a> as the frontrunner candidates, and projected that they would join by 2025, during the next mandate of the European Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Negotiations with Turkey are ongoing, but the pace has slowed due to objections from the EU to the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%93present_purges_in_Turkey" title="2016\xe2\x80\x93present purges in Turkey">Turkish government\'s response</a> to the <a href="/wiki/2016_Turkish_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="2016 Turkish coup d&#39;\xc3\xa9tat attempt">2016 coup d\'\xc3\xa9tat attempt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" Union</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">Brexit</a></li></ul></li></ul>\n<hr />\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Microstates_and_the_European_Union" title="Microstates and the European Nations</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Union_Association_Agreement" title="European Union Association Agreement">European Union Association Agreement</a></li></ul>\n<hr />\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Group_of_Seven" title="Group of Seven">G7</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a></li></ul></div></div></td>\n</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-below">\n<a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Europe.svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of Europe.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/32px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="21" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/48px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/64px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="540" /></a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Portal:European_Union" title="Portal:European Union">European Union&#32;portal</a> <div class="hlist" style="text-align:center;font-weight:normal;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_political_science#Politics_by_region" title="Outline of political science">Other countries</a></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r992953826">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox .navbar{display:block;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox-title .navbar{float:left;text-align:left;margin-right:0.5em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_the_European_Union" title="Template:Politics of the European Union"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_the_European_Union" title="Template talk:Politics of the European Union"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">EU treaties</a>, membership of the European Union is open to "any European State which respects the values referred to in Article 2 and is committed to promoting them" (<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Consolidated_version_of_the_Treaty_on_European_Union/Title_VI:_Final_Provisions#Article_49" class="extiw" title="s:Consolidated version of the Treaty on European Union/Title VI: Final Provisions">TEU Article 49</a>). Those <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Consolidated_version_of_the_Treaty_on_European_Union/Title_I:_Common_Provisions#Article_2" class="extiw" title="s:Consolidated version of the Treaty on European Union/Title I: Common Provisions">Article 2</a> values are "respect for human dignity, freedom, democracy, equality, the rule of law and respect for human rights, including the rights of persons belonging to minorities." This is based on the 1993 "<a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_criteria" title="Copenhagen criteria">Copenhagen criteria</a>" agreed as it became clear many former <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> countries would apply to join;\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Membership requires that candidate country has achieved stability of institutions guaranteeing <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a>, respect for and protection of <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">minorities</a>, the existence of a functioning <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a> as well as the capacity to cope with competitive pressure and market forces within the Union. Membership presupposes the candidate\'s ability to take on the obligations of membership including adherence to the aims of political, economic and <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_Monetary_Union_of_the_European_Union" title="Economic and Monetary Union of the European Union">monetary</a> union.</p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite>Excerpt from the Copenhagen Presidency conclusions<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>\n<p>In December 1995, the Madrid European Council revised the membership criteria to include conditions for member country integration through the appropriate adjustment of its administrative structures: since it is important that European Community legislation be reflected in national legislation, it is critical that the revised national legislation be implemented effectively through appropriate administrative and judicial structures.\n</p><p>Finally, and technically outside the Copenhagen criteria, comes the further requirement that all prospective members must enact legislation to bring their laws into line with the body of European law built up over the history of the Union, known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Acquis_communautaire" title="Acquis communautaire">acquis communautaire</a></i>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Process">Process</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Process">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belgique_-_Bruxelles_-_Schuman_-_Berlaymont_-_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Belgique_-_Bruxelles_-_Schuman_-_Berlaymont_-_01.jpg/220px-Belgique_-_Bruxelles_-_Schuman_-_Berlaymont_-_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Belgique_-_Bruxelles_-_Schuman_-_Berlaymont_-_01.jpg/330px-Belgique_-_Bruxelles_-_Schuman_-_Berlaymont_-_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Belgique_-_Bruxelles_-_Schuman_-_Berlaymont_-_01.jpg/440px-Belgique_-_Bruxelles_-_Schuman_-_Berlaymont_-_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5180" data-file-height="2894" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belgique_-_Bruxelles_-_Schuman_-_Berlaymont_-_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The European Commission, which plays a central role in the enlargement process.</div></div></div>\n<p>Today the accession process follows a series of formal steps, from a pre-accession agreement to the ratification of the final accession treaty. These steps are primarily presided over by the European Commission (<a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_Enlargement_and_European_Neighbourhood_Policy" class="mw-redirect" title="European Commissioner for Enlargement and European Neighbourhood Policy">Enlargement Commissioner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Directorate-General_for_Enlargement_(European_Commission)" class="mw-redirect" title="Directorate-General for Enlargement (European Commission)">DG Enlargement</a>), but the actual negotiations are technically conducted between the Union\'s Member States and the candidate country.\n</p><p>Before a country applies for membership it typically signs an <a href="/wiki/Association_agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Association agreement">association agreement</a> to help prepare the country for candidacy and eventual membership. Most countries do not meet the criteria to even begin negotiations before they apply, so they need many years to prepare for the process. An association agreement helps prepare for this first step.\n</p><p>In the case of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Balkans" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Balkans">Western Balkans</a>, a special process, the <a href="/wiki/Stabilisation_and_Association_Process" title="Stabilisation and Association Process">Stabilisation and Association Process</a> exists to deal with the special circumstances there.\n</p><p>When a country formally applies for membership, the Council asks the commission to prepare an opinion on the country\'s readiness to begin negotiations. The council can then either accept or reject the commission\'s opinion (The council has only once rejected the commission\'s opinion when the latter advised against opening negotiations with Greece).<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>If the Council agrees to open negotiations the screening process then begins. The commission and candidate country examine its laws and those of the EU and determine what differences exist. The Council then recommends opening negotiations on "chapters" of law that it feels there is sufficient common ground to have constructive negotiations. Negotiations are typically a matter of the candidate country convincing the EU that its laws and administrative capacity are sufficient to execute European law, which can be implemented as seen fit by the member states. Often this will involve time-lines before the Acquis Communautaire (European regulations, <a href="/wiki/Directive_(European_Union)" title="Directive (European Union)">directives</a> &amp; standards) has to be fully implemented.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EU-GDP-Population.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/EU-GDP-Population.svg/250px-EU-GDP-Population.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/EU-GDP-Population.svg/375px-EU-GDP-Population.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/EU-GDP-Population.svg/500px-EU-GDP-Population.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EU-GDP-Population.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population and GDP per capita of individual EU member states compared with those of non-member states in Europe.</div></div></div>\n<p>A chapter is said to be closed when both sides have agreed it has been implemented sufficiently, however it can still be re-opened if the Commission feels that the candidate has fallen out of compliance.\n</p><p>To assess progress achieved by countries in preparing for accession to the European Union, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> submits regular reports (yearly) to the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>. These serve as a basis for the council to make decisions on negotiations or their extension to other candidates.\n</p><p>Once the negotiations are complete, a <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Accession" title="Treaty of Accession">Treaty of Accession</a> will be signed, which must then be ratified by all of the member states of the Union, as well as the institutions of the Union, and the candidate country. Once this has been completed it will join the Union on the date specified in the treaty.\n</p><p>The entire process, from application for membership to membership has typically taken about a decade, although some countries, notably Sweden, Finland, and Austria have been faster, taking only a few years. The process from application for association agreement through accession has taken far longer, as much as several decades (Turkey for example first applied for association in the 1950s and has yet to conclude accession negotiations).\n</p><p>On 18 October 2019, France vetoed starting of negotiations with Albania and North Macedonia, citing problems with current enlargement process.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In November 2019, France proposed a seven-stage accession plan for membership.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The reformed accession strategy proposes participation in different programs, such as Erasmus, Banking Union, Capital Markets Union, Customs Union, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Example">Example</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Example">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following is an example of the accession process\xe2\x80\x94Estonia\'s path to membership from its <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Restoration_of_Independence" title="Estonian Restoration of Independence">declaration of independence</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> in November 1991 with recognition from the EU the same month to <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Accession_2003" title="Treaty of Accession 2003">membership</a> in May 2004. Ease of accession depends on the state: how integrated it is with the EU beforehand, the state of its economy and public institutions, any outstanding political issues with the EU and (historically) how much law to date the EU has built up that the acceding state must adopt. This outline also includes integration steps taken by the accession country after it attains membership.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Estonia EU membership timeline\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Year\n</th>\n<th style="width:100px;">Date\n</th>\n<th>Event\n</th>\n<th>Notes\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1991\n</td>\n<td>20 August\n</td>\n<td>Declaration of abolished restrictions before 2011\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Success_and_fatigue">Success and fatigue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Success and fatigue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Enlargement has been one of the EU\'s most successful foreign policies,<sup id="cite_ref-ISS_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISS-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> yet has equally suffered from considerable opposition from the start. <a href="/wiki/President_of_France" title="President of France">French President</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> opposed British membership.<sup id="cite_ref-Bache_1_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bache_1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> A later French President <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Mitterrand" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois Mitterrand">Fran\xc3\xa7ois Mitterrand</a> opposed Greek, Spanish and Portuguese membership fearing that the former dictatorships were not ready and it would reduce the union to a free-trade area.<sup id="cite_ref-ESI_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESI-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The reasons for the first member states to apply, and for them to be accepted, were primarily economic while the second enlargement was more political. The southern Mediterranean countries had just emerged from dictatorships and wanted to secure their democratic systems through the EEC, while the EEC wanted to ensure the same thing and that their southern neighbours were stable and aligned to NATO.<sup id="cite_ref-Bache_1_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bache_1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> These two principal forces, economic gain and political security, have been behind enlargements since. However, with the recent large enlargements in 2004, public opinion in Europe has turned against further expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-ESI_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESI-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It has also been acknowledged that enlargement has its limits; the EU cannot expand endlessly.<sup id="cite_ref-ISS_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISS-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">Commission President</a> <a href="/wiki/Romano_Prodi" title="Romano Prodi">Romano Prodi</a> favoured granting "everything but institutions" to the EU\'s neighbour states, allowing them to co-operate deeply while not adding strain on the EU\'s institutional framework.<sup id="cite_ref-ISS_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISS-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> This has in particular been pushed by France and Germany as a <a href="/wiki/Privileged_partnership" title="Privileged partnership">privileged partnership</a> for Turkey, membership for which has faced considerable opposition on cultural and logistical grounds.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_enlargements">Historical enlargements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Historical enlargements">edit</a><span href="#cite_note-Enlargement-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="line-height:92%; text-align:left" rowspan="3"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom"><img alt="United Kingdom" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="12" href="/wiki/Accession_of_the_United_Kingdom_to_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Accession of the United Kingdom to the European Union">United Kingdom</a>\n</th>\n<td style="line-height:92%; text-align:right">1961-08-10\n</td>\n<td style="line-height:92%; text-align:right; background:#FFADB7"><div class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" style="background:transparent;text-align:left;;">\nby France</div></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="line-height:92%; text-align:right">1967-05-10\n</td>\n<td style="line-height:92%; style="background:transparent;text-align:left;;">\nfollowing <a href="/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2016 United Kingdom European Union membership href="/wiki/Statistics_relating_to_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Statistics relating to enlargement of the European Union">Statistics relating to enlargement of the European Union</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding_members">Founding members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Founding members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a> (ECSC) was proposed by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Schuman" title="Robert Schuman">Robert Schuman</a> in <a href="/wiki/Schuman_Declaration" title="Schuman Declaration">his declaration</a> on <a href="/wiki/Europe_Day" title="Europe Day">9 May 1950</a> and involved the pooling of the <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a> industries of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Half of the project states, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, had already achieved a great degree of integration amongst themselves with the organs of <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a> and earlier bilateral agreements. These five countries were joined by <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and they all signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1951)" title="Treaty of Paris (1951)">Treaty of Paris</a> on 23 July 1952. These six members, dubbed the \'<a href="/wiki/Inner_Six" title="Inner Six">inner six</a>\' (as opposed to the \'<a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association#Former_members" title="European Free Trade Association">outer seven</a>\' who formed the <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">European Free Trade Association</a> who were suspicious of such plans for integration) went on to sign the <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_Rome" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaties of Rome">Treaties of Rome</a> establishing two further communities, together known as the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a> when they merged their executives in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-janse18_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-janse18-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1962, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Military_dictator" class="mw-redirect" title="Military dictator">military dictator</a> <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a>, issued its first attempt to join the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a>. Spanish Foreign Affairs minister <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Mar%C3%ADa_Castiella" title="Fernando Mar\xc3\xada Castiella">Fernando Mar\xc3\xada Castiella</a> sent the request form to French Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Couve_de_Murville" title="Maurice Couve de Murville">Maurice Couve de Murville</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> This request was rejected by all the member countries in 1964; <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">Spain was not a democracy</a> at the time, and thus unable to enter the EEC.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Community did see some loss of territory due to the <a href="/wiki/Decolonialisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Decolonialisation">decolonialisation</a> occurring in their era. <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, which was an integral part of France, had a special relationship with the Community.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Algeria gained independence on 5 July 1962 and hence left the Community. There was no enlargement until the 1970s.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_enlargement">First enlargement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: First enlargement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1973_enlargement_of_the_European_Communities" title="1973 enlargement of the European Communities">1973 enlargement of the European Communities</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, which had refused to join as a founding member, changed its policy following the <a href="/wiki/Suez_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Suez crisis">Suez crisis</a> and applied to be a member of the Communities. Other EEC members were also inclined to British membership on those grounds. <a href="/wiki/French_President" class="mw-redirect" title="French President">French President</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> vetoed British membership.<sup id="cite_ref-Bache_1_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bache_1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Once de Gaulle had left office, the door to enlargement was once again opened. The EEC economy had also slowed down and British membership was seen as a way to revitalise the community.<sup id="cite_ref-Bache_1_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bache_1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Only after a 12-hour talk between British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Edward_Heath" title="Edward Heath">Edward Heath</a> and French President <a href="/wiki/Georges_Pompidou" title="Georges Pompidou">Georges Pompidou</a> took place did Britain\'s third application succeed.<sup id="cite_ref-upi.com_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upi.com-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> After Britain was accepted Prime Minister Edward Heath said:\n</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>"For my part, I have no doubt at all that the discussions which we have had will prove of real and lasting benefit, not only to Britain and France, but to Europe as a whole."<sup id="cite_ref-upi.com_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upi.com-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p>As part of the deal for British entry, France agreed to allow the EEC its own monetary resources. However France made that concession only as Britain\'s small agriculture sector would ensure that Britain would be a net contributor to the <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">Common Agricultural Policy</a> dominated <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">EEC budget</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bache_1_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bache_1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Applying together with the UK, as on the previous occasions, were <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> These countries were so economically linked to the UK that they considered it necessary to join the EEC if the UK did.<sup id="cite_ref-Bache_1_14-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bache_1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> However the Norwegian government <a href="/wiki/1972_Norwegian_European_Communities_membership_referendum" title="1972 Norwegian European Communities membership referendum">lost a national referendum on membership</a> and hence did not accede with the others on 1 January 1973. <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> joined the Community with the United Kingdom at this point, as can be seen in the long title of the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities_Act_1972_(UK)" title="European Communities Act 1972 (UK)">UK European Communities Act 1972</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mediterranean_enlargements">Mediterranean enlargements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Mediterranean enlargements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/1981_enlargement_of_the_European_Communities" title="1981 enlargement of the European Communities">1981 enlargement of the European Communities</a> and <a href="/wiki/1986_enlargement_of_the_European_Communities" title="1986 enlargement of the European Communities">1986 enlargement of the European Communities</a></div>\n<p>The next enlargement would occur for different reasons. The 1970s also saw <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> emerge from dictatorship. These countries desired to consolidate their new democratic systems by binding themselves into the EEC. Equally, the EEC was unsure about which way these countries were heading and wanted to ensure stability along its southern borders.<sup id="cite_ref-Bache_1_14-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bache_1-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> However <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Mitterrand" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois Mitterrand">Fran\xc3\xa7ois Mitterrand</a> initially opposed their membership fearing they were not ready and it would water the community down to a free trade area.<sup id="cite_ref-ESI_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESI-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Greece joined the EU in 1981 followed by Spain and Portugal in 1986.\n</p><p>The year 1985, however, saw the first time a territory voted to <a href="/wiki/Withdrawal_from_the_European_Union" title="Withdrawal from the European Union">leave the Community</a>, when <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> was granted <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">home rule</a> by Denmark and the territory used its new powers and voted to withdraw from the Community (See <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_the_European_Union" title="Special member state territories and the European Union">member state territories</a>).\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> applied for membership in 1987. Morocco\'s application was turned down as it was not considered European, while Turkey\'s application was considered eligible on the basis of the 1963 <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Association_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Ankara Association Agreement">Ankara Association Agreement</a>, but the opinion of the commission on the possible candidate status was by then negative. Turkey received candidate status only in 1999 and began official membership negotiations in 2005, which are still in progress as of 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Post.E2.80.93Cold_War"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post\xe2\x80\x93Cold_War">Post\xe2\x80\x93Cold War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Post\xe2\x80\x93Cold War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1995_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="1995 enlargement of the European Union">1995 enlargement of the European Union</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg/220px-West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg/330px-West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg/440px-West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg 2x" data-file-width="661" data-file-height="498" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a>\'s fall enabled eastward enlargement. (<a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a>)</div></div></div>\n<p>After the 1970s, Europe experienced an economic downturn which led to leaders launching of the <a href="/wiki/Single_European_Act" title="Single European Act">Single European Act</a> which set to create a single market by 1992. The effect of this was that <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">EFTA</a> states found it harder to export to the EEC and businesses (including large EFTA corporations such as <a href="/wiki/Volvo" title="Volvo">Volvo</a>) wished to relocate within the new single market making the downturn worse for EFTA. EFTA states began to discuss closer links with the EEC despite its domestic unpopularity.<sup id="cite_ref-Bache_2_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bache_2-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> were neutral in the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> so membership of an organisation developing a <a href="/wiki/Common_foreign_and_security_policy" class="mw-redirect" title="Common foreign and security policy">common foreign and security policy</a> would be incompatible with that. With the end of the Cold War in 1989, that obstacle was removed, and the desire to pursue membership grew stronger.<sup id="cite_ref-Bache_2_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bache_2-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On 3 October 1990, the <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">reunification of East and West Germany</a> brought East Germany into the Community without increasing the number of member states.\n</p><p>The Community later became the European Union in 1993 by virtue of the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a>, and established standards for new entrants so their suitability could be judged. The <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_criteria" title="Copenhagen criteria">Copenhagen criteria</a> stated in 1993 that a country must be a <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a>, operate a <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free market</a>, and be willing to adopt the entire body of <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Law of the European Union">EU law</a> already agreed upon. Also in 1993 the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a> was established with the EFTA states except <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>. Most of the new EEA states pursued full EU membership as the EEA did not sufficiently satisfy the needs of their export based corporations. The EU has also preferred these states to integrate via the EEA rather than full membership as the EEC wished to pursue <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">monetary integration</a> and did not wish for another round of enlargement to occupy their attention. However, with the EEA\'s credibility dented following rejection by businesses and Switzerland, the EU agreed with full membership. This was more readily accepted with the prospect of poorer countries wishing to join; contributions from richer countries would help balance the EU budget.<sup id="cite_ref-Bache_2_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bache_2-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On 1 January 1995 <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> acceded to the EU marking its fourth enlargement. The Norwegian government lost a second national referendum on membership.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_enlargement">Eastern enlargement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Eastern enlargement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">2004 enlargement of the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/2007_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2007 enlargement of the European Union">2007 enlargement of the European Union</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EU2004-2013.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/dc/EU2004-2013.svg/220px-EU2004-2013.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/dc/EU2004-2013.svg/330px-EU2004-2013.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/dc/EU2004-2013.svg/440px-EU2004-2013.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2285" data-file-height="2445" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EU2004-2013.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>EU\'s enlargements in the 2000s and the 2010s:<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#009900; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;European Union 1 Jan. 1995&#160;&#8211;&#32;30 April 2004</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#33CC33; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Joined the EU on 1 May 2004</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#66FF66; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Joined the EU on 1 Jan. 2007</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#B9FF83; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Joined the EU on 1 July 2013</div></div></div></div>\n<p>As with the Mediterranean countries in the 1980s, the countries in <a href="/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe" title="Central and Eastern Europe">Central and Eastern Europe</a> had emerged from dictatorships and wanted to consolidate their democracies. They also wanted to join the project of European integration and ensure they did not fall back into the <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> sphere of influence. The EU and NATO offered a guarantee of this, and the EU was also seen as vital to ensuring the economic success of those countries. However, the EU\'s desire to accept these countries\' membership applications was less than rapid. The collapse of communism came quickly and was not anticipated. The EU struggled to deal with the sudden reunification of Germany with the addition of its poorer 17 million people and, while keeping its monetary union project on track, it was still at that early stage pointing the EFTA countries in the direction of the EEA rather than full membership.<sup id="cite_ref-Bache_3_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bache_3-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>States in Central and Eastern Europe persisted and eventually the above-mentioned issues were cleared. The US also pressured the EU to offer membership as a temporary guarantee; it feared expanding NATO too rapidly for fear of frightening Russia. Although eventually trying to limit the number of members, and after encouragement from the US, the EU pursued talks with ten countries and a change of mind<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (March 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> by <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> helped to offset slightly the influx of large poorer member states from Central and Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Bache_3_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bache_3-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the end, eight Central and Eastern European countries (the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>), plus two <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a> countries (<a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>) were able to join on 1 May 2004. This was the largest single enlargement in terms of people, and number of countries, though not in terms of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The less developed nature of these countries was of concern to some of the older member states. Some countries, such as the UK, immediately opened their job market to the accession states, whereas most others placed temporary restrictions on the rights of work of the citizens of these states to their countries. The movement westward of some of the labour force of the newly acceded countries that occurred in the aftermath of the enlargement initially spawned clich\xc3\xa9s among the public opinion and media of some western countries (such as the "<a href="/wiki/Polish_plumber" title="Polish plumber">Polish plumber</a>"), despite the generally conceded benefit to the economies concerned.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The official EU media (the speeches of the European Commission) frequently referred to the enlargement to the CEE region as "an historical opportunity" and "morally imperative", which reflected the desire of the EU to admit these countries as members, even though they were less developed than the Western European countries.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\nFollowing this <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, though were deemed initially as not fully ready by the commission to join in 2004, acceded nevertheless on 1 January 2007. These, like the countries joining in 2004, faced a series of restrictions as to their citizens not fully enjoying working rights on the territory of some of the older EU members. Bulgaria and Romania are not yet members of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen area</a>; however, their citizens can travel visa-free to the other EU countries.\n</p><p>The socio-economic research on the attitudes towards the integration from both hosting and visiting countries has revealed divergent views. The analysis shows, there are a number of possible factors of the rationalization and understanding of the practices on what the enlargement has been and should be like. Attitudes of even skeptical citizens, do not discard the possibility on future sustainable enlargements. The years subsequent to the EU accession will lead to extensive dialogues between policy-makers, governments, and European citizens about the path for a constructive development.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_Balkans_enlargements">Western Balkans enlargements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Western Balkans enlargements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2013 enlargement of the European Union">2013 enlargement of the European Union</a></div>\n<p>The 2003 European Council summit in <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a> set integration of the Western <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> as a priority of EU expansion. The EU\'s relations with the <a href="/wiki/Western_Balkans" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Balkans">Western Balkans</a> states were moved from the "<a href="/wiki/Directorate-General_for_External_Relations_(European_Commission)" title="Directorate-General for External Relations (European Commission)">External Relations</a>" to the "<a href="/wiki/Directorate-General_for_Enlargement" class="mw-redirect" title="Directorate-General for Enlargement">Enlargement</a>" policy segment in 2005. Those states which have not been recognised as candidate countries are considered "potential candidate countries".<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The move to <a href="/wiki/Directorate-General_for_Enlargement" class="mw-redirect" title="Directorate-General for Enlargement">Enlargement directorate</a> was a consequence of the advancement of the <a href="/wiki/Stabilisation_and_Association_process" class="mw-redirect" title="Stabilisation and Association process">Stabilisation and Association process</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> joined on 1 July 2013, following ratification of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Accession_2011" title="Treaty of Accession 2011">2011 Accession Treaty</a> by all other EU countries. <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> and the several successor states of the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a> have all adopted EU integration as an aim of foreign policy.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Detail">Detail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Jersey, Guernsey\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline">Timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="mw-headline" id="Current_enlargement_agenda">Current enlargement agenda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Current enlargement agenda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Potential_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Potential enlargement of the European Union">Potential enlargement of the European Union</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Union_Members.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/European_Union_Members.svg/300px-European_Union_Members.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/European_Union_Members.svg/450px-European_Union_Members.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/European_Union_Members.svg/600px-European_Union_Members.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="610" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Union_Members.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#3366FF; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;current members</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#33CC33; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;candidate members</div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#FFCC00; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;potential members</div></div></div></div>\n<p>Article 49 of the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a> (as amended) says that any European state that respects the "principles of liberty, democracy, respect for human rights and fundamental freedoms, and the rule of law", may apply to join the Union. The <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> set out the conditions for EU membership in June 1993 in the so-called <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_criteria" title="Copenhagen criteria">Copenhagen criteria</a> (see <a href="#Criteria">Criteria</a> above for details). The Western <a href="/wiki/Balkan" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan">Balkan</a> states had to sign <a href="/wiki/Stabilisation_and_Association_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Stabilisation and Association Agreement">Stabilisation and Association Agreements</a> (SAAs) before applying for membership.\n</p><p>Turkey <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Turkey_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Turkey to the European Union">applied for membership</a> in 1987.  The Western Balkans have been prioritised for membership since emerging from war during the <a href="/wiki/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia" title="Breakup of Yugoslavia">breakup of Yugoslavia</a> in the early 1990s. <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_North_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> are all recognized as official candidates and in <a href="/wiki/Negotiation" title="Negotiation">negotiation</a>, negotiations with <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> are frozen.<sup id="cite_ref-status_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-status-98">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>*<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> are recognized as potential candidates for membership by the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-status_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-status-98">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Bosnia has submitted an application for EU membership, while Bosnia and Kosovo have an SAA with the EU.\n</p><p>In July 2014, <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">President of the European Commission</a> <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker" title="Jean-Claude Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</a> announced that the EU has no plans to expand in the next five years.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Juncker has described <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> as front-runner candidates, and projected that they would join by 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> endorsed starting negotiations with <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> on 26 March 2020, and they could join after 2025. <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> is not expected to join anytime soon.\n</p><p>On 6 February 2018, the European Commission published its expansion plan,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> which covers the six Western Balkan countries. The plan envisages that all six applicants could achieve accession as members of the European Union after 2025. In May 2018, Bulgaria\xe2\x80\x94holding the rotating <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_the_Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Presidency of the Council of the European Union">presidency of the Council of the European Union</a>\xe2\x80\x94hosted a summit on the Western Balkans, which aimed to facilitate accession by the six, including enhanced regional security cooperation and regional connectivity.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It was noteworthy that the Summit referred to \'partners\' rather than states: this reflects that Kosovo is <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">partially recognised</a> as a state.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> As of 2018, Kosovo was not recognized by fellow Western Balkan applicant Serbia, and existing EU members <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>. The European Commission is sensitive to the issue which was addressed in a speech by the EU\'s High Representative/Vice-President <a href="/wiki/Federica_Mogherini" title="Federica Mogherini">Federica Mogherini</a> at the European Parliament Plenary Session on the Western Balkan Strategy: " shared, unequivocal, concrete perspective for European Union integration for each and every one of the six partners. Each at its own pace, with its own specificities and under different conditions, but the direction is clear and is one".<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cancelled_enlargements">Cancelled enlargements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Cancelled enlargements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Not all enlargement negotiations have ended with the accession of a new member state. <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> completed membership negotiations twice, in 1972 and 1994, but both times membership was rejected in a referendum. <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> applied for membership in May 1992 but subsequently froze its application,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> and formally withdrew it in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> lodged its application following an economic collapse in 2008, but froze accession negotiations in 2013. In 2017, Iceland\'s newly elected government announced that it may seek to begin talks with the EU on possible future membership once again,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> but this did not happen as the government survived for only eight months. New elections were called in October 2017, leading to a new left\xe2\x80\x93right coalition government in November 2017. Following the elections, all the parties of the governing coalition oppose EU membership, along with two of the opposition parties, summing up to at least two-thirds of the MPs. Additionally, for more than eight years every single opinion poll published in Iceland has had a solid majority against joining the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-Very_long_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-very_long" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>may be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Article_size" title="Wikipedia:Article size">too long</a> to read and navigate comfortably</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please consider <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Splitting" title="Wikipedia:Splitting">splitting</a> content into sub-articles, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Summary_style" title="Wikipedia:Summary style">condensing</a> it, or adding <a href="/wiki/Help:Section#Subsections" title="Help:Section">subheadings</a>. Please discuss this issue on the article\'s <a href="/wiki/Talk:Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Talk:Enlargement of the European Union">talk page</a>.</span>  <small class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-BER-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-BER_54-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Until the <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Germany" title="Unification of Germany">unification of Germany</a> in 1990 the <i>de jure</i> status of <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a> was that of French, UK and US occupied zones with <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West German</a> civilian administration. The treaties applied fully during 1952\xe2\x80\x931990 over the West German and French responsibilities, and during 1973\xe2\x80\x931990 over the UK responsibilities. From 3 October 1990 <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a> was fully integrated in the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Republic_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Republic of Germany">Federal Republic of Germany</a> along with <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-FP-55"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FP_55-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Renamed French Polynesia on 1957-07-22</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-VU-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-VU_56-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-VU_56-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-VU_56-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The New Hebrides was a <a href="/wiki/Condominium_(international_law)" title="Condominium (international law)">condominium</a> between the United Kingdom and France until its independence in 1980, and was generally considered to be an overseas territory of both countries</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-IND-57"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-IND_57-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Became part of India on 1954-07-21</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-TAF-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-TAF_58-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Ad\xc3\xa9lie Land, Crozet Islands, Kerguelen Islands and Saint-Paul-and-Amsterdam Islands merged to become the French Southern and Antarctic Lands on 1955-08-06. All territories were already outside the ECSC and the merged territory retained the same status</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-TOG-59"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-TOG_59-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Renamed Togo on 1958-02-22</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-MAL-60"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-MAL_60-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Renamed Sudanese Republic on 1958-11-24</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-SRS-61"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-SRS_61-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-SRS_61-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Senegal and the Sudanese Republic merged on 1959-04-04 to create the Mali Federation</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-MR-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-MR_62-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Renamed Malagasy Republic on 1958-10-14</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-MC-63"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-MC_63-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Renamed Congo on 1958-11-28</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-SAI-64"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-SAI_64-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Renamed French Territory of the Afars and the Issas in 1967</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-RB-65"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-RB_65-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Became independent as the Kingdom of Ruanda and the Kingdom of Burundi</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-NNG-66"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-NNG_66-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Annexed by Indonesia in 1962</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-DG-69"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-DG_69-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Including the County of Greenland, which later gained home rule and left the EC</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-CEK-70"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-CEK_70-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The UK co-administered the condominium of the Canton and Enderbury Islands with the USA, until the UK merged it with its Gilbert and Ellice Islands colony on 1975-01-01 to create its Gilbert Islands colony. As such it ceased to be a condominium, but the USA continued to claim it until 1979</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-BBH-71"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-BBH_71-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Renamed Belize on 1973-06-01</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-BSI-72"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-BSI_72-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Renamed the British Solomon Islands on 1976-01-02</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-SGI-73"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-SGI_73-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Renamed South Georgia and the South Sandwich Islands in 1985</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-GEI-74"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-GEI_74-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Split into the Gilbert Islands (which was merged with the Canton and Enderbury Islands) and Ellice Island on 1975-01-01</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-AD-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-AD_75-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">British Sovereign Base Areas on the island of Cyprus</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-RZ-76"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-RZ_76-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Legally a British colony until independence in 1980</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-AAB-77"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-AAB_77-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The island of Barbuda became a separate territory from Antigua on 1976-12-23</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-COM-78"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-COM_78-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-COM_78-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The island of Mayotte became a separate territory in 1974, and chose to remain with France, rather than become independent</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-CNA-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-CNA_79-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-CNA_79-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Anguilla stayed a British colony, while Saint Christopher and Nevis became independent as St. Kitts and Nevis</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-ABR-80"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ABR_80-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Antigua, Barbuda and Redonda merged to become independent as Antigua and Barbuda</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-ARB-82"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ARB_82-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although Aruba was only added to the OCT list with the entry into force of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Amsterdam" title="Treaty of Amsterdam">Treaty of Amsterdam</a> in 1999, it was considered an OCT by the European Communities since leaving the Netherlands Antilles: "De eilandgebieden zullen dus de rechten en plichten van de LGO-status van het Land de Nederlandse Antillen overnemen, wanneer dat opgeheven wordt. Hetzelfde gebeurde in 1986 toen Aruba van eilandgebied van de Nederlandse Antillen een apart Land binnen het Koninkrijk werd. Hoewel de LGO-bijlage pas in 1999 aan deze situatie werd aangepast, heeft de Europese Gemeenschap Aruba van het begin af aan als LGO behandeld." in: Dutch Ministry of Foreign Affairs<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-NEA-83"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-NEA_83-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-NEA_83-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The Netherlands Antilles dissolved on 10 October 2010 and contained the islands of Aruba (which left the Netherlands Antilles in 1986), Bonaire, Curacao, Sint Maarten, Saba and Sint Eustatius. Aruba, Curacao and Sint Maarten are autonomous countries in the Kingdom of Netherlands, and remain overseas territories of the European Union. Bonaire, St Eustatius and Saba, also known as the <a href="/wiki/BES_islands" class="mw-redirect" title="BES islands">BES islands</a>, are special municipalities of the Netherlands, and remained legally overseas territories</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-ETL-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ETL_84-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>De jure</i> a Portuguese colony under Indonesian occupation until 1999</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-CH-85"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-CH_85-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-CH_85-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Transferred to China</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-GBM-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-GBM_88-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Saint Martin and Saint Barth\xc3\xa9lemy were part of Guadeloupe and thus already part of the EU. On 2007-02-22, they became separate territories but France retained application of EU law there, and their EU OMR status was confirmed in the Treaty of Lisbon, which entered into force on 2009-01-01.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-TAA-89"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-TAA_89-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Scattered islands in the Indian Ocean became part of the French Southern and Antarctic Lands on 2007-02-22. Both territories were already EU OCTs and the merged territory retained the same status.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1011085734"/><div class="reflist">\n</div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1011085734"/><div class="reflist reflist-columns references-column-width" style="column-width: 30em;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Current Article 1 of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Maastricht" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Maastricht">Treaty on European Union</a> reads:"The Union shall be founded on the present Treaty and on the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union</a>. Those <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_EU" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaties of the EU">two Treaties</a> shall have the same legal value. The Union shall replace and succeed the <a href="/wiki/European_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="European Community">European Community</a>".</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-auto-2"><span Retrieved <span class="nowrap">27 June</span> 2014</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Enlargement+-+Check+current+status&amp;rft.pub=European+Commission&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fec.europa.eu%2Fenlargement%2Fcountries%2Fcheck-current-status%2Findex_en.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEnlargement+of+the+European+Union" class="Z3988"></span></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-99"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-99">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Kosovo is the subject of a territorial dispute between the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Kosovo" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Kosovo">Republic of Kosovo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Serbia" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Serbia">Republic of Serbia</a>. The Republic of Kosovo <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">unilaterally declared independence</a> on 17 February 2008. <a href="/wiki/Kosovo%E2%80%93Serbia_relations" title="Kosovo\xe2\x80\x93Serbia relations">Serbia continues to claim</a> it as part of its <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">own sovereign territory</a>. The two governments <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Pristina_negotiations" title="Belgrade\xe2\x80\x93Pristina negotiations">began to normalise relations</a> in 2013, as part of the <a href="/wiki/2013_Brussels_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="2013 Brussels Agreement">2013 Brussels Agreement</a>. Kosovo is currently <i>(this note self-updates)</i> recognized as an independent state by <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">98</a> out of the 193 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_member_states" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations member states">United Nations member states</a>. In total, <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">113</a> UN member states recognized Kosovo at some point, of which <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">15</a> later withdrew their recognition.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-100"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-100">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.heraldscotland.com/politics/referendum-news/better-together-junckers-eu-comments-harm-yes-camp.1405434338">"Better Together accused in Juncker row"</a>. <i>Herald Scotland</i>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Herald+Scotland&amp;rft.atitle=Better+Together+accused+in+Juncker+row&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.heraldscotland.com%2Fpolitics%2Freferendum-news%2Fbetter-together-junckers-eu-comments-harm-yes-camp.1405434338&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEnlargement+of+the+European+Union" class="Z3988"></span></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-101"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-101">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://ec.europa.eu/commission/news/strategy-western-balkans-2018-feb-06_en">"Strategy for the Western Balkans"</a>. <i>Europa: European Commission</i>. 6 February 2018<span class="reference-accessdate">.
